item_0.episode_type: litigation_correspondence
item_0.note: Defense counsel Aletha Thomas initiated mediation discussion on December 1, 2025. Plaintiff responded December 10, 2025 requesting EDR (Electronic Data Recorder) data from commercial vehicle before proceeding to mediation. Defense confirmed December 15, 2025 that no EDR download exists for this incident. Plaintiff responded January 12, 2026 requesting formal verified interrogatory responses stating under oath: (1) No EDR download was performed, (2) Whether vehicle was equipped with EDR system, (3) If equipped, why no download was performed, (4) Whether any EDR data was overwritten, deleted, or destroyed. This is critical given defendant Hamilton's conflicting deposition testimony claiming no contact occurred and damage was from truck stop hit-and-run, despite photos showing damage to front passenger corner consistent with plaintiff's account of semi merging into her vehicle.

- The thread includes the standard attorney-client privilege disclosure included in each electronic message, stating that the message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain privileged information; recipients who receive the message in error should contact the sender and refrain from sharing or using the contents.

Please advise when we may expect responses.” The communication pattern shows ongoing efforts to obtain supplemental discovery responses related to EDR information.

Thomas at Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC, with copies to Nichole M. Priddy and Alma Cristobal’s Filevine project email address, and included the same business contact details for The Whaley Law Firm as in prior messages. - Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC: Aletha N. Thomas, Partner; Offices listed in Kentucky (and other states), with direct line, cell, and general contact channels in the signature block of the May 28, 2025 correspondence.

item_53.note: Case: Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024 concerns Alma Cristobal, born [DOB-1], in a motor vehicle accident matter. The note set documents an ongoing Certified Medical Records and Billing request, with a detailed email chain between The Whaley Law Firm and Aptiva Health.

On January 21, 2025, Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Dorothy Brown at Aptiva Health, copying Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm. In that message, she stated that, after reviewing the attached records for Alma Cristobal, the first few visits appear to be missing: specifically the dates [DOB-113], [DOB-114], and [DOB-115]. She requested that those dates of service be added and that the package be sent with a corrected certification page. The message included Sarena’s contact details, noting a new email address (sarena@whaleylawfirm.com) and listing her direct and office lines, as well as The Whaley Law Firm’s mailing address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. It also reiterated that Dorothy Brown’s communication should be sent from the Aptiva Health address and that Bryce Koon should be cc’d; the subject line again referenced Certified Medical Records & Billing Request for Alma Cristobal, DOB [DOB-1].

The historical thread begins with a July 23, 2024 email in which Sarena requested certified medical records and billing for Alma Cristobal (DOB [DOB-1]). On July 29, 2024, Dorothy Brown replied that she had attached the updated records and bills, along with the certification page. Shortly thereafter, there was back-and-forth about the certification page: on July 30, 2024, Dorothy wrote, “Sorry about that. Here is that certification page.” In the same exchange, Sarena indicated that, upon review, it appeared the certification page was still missing and asked Dorothy to forward it; Dorothy subsequently responded with a confirmation that the certification page had been sent, and Sarena acknowledged receipt. The dated sequence shows multiple confirmations and acknowledgments around the certification page and the accompanying records.

In an ongoing process later in 2024, on September 26, 2024, Sarena explained that Alma had returned to Aptiva in August for follow-up visits and asked Dorothy to update the request and certification with those new records and billing. Dorothy responded on September 27, 2024 by providing updated records and bills, along with the certification page. On September 30, 2024, Sarena acknowledged receipt of those updated materials.

This sequence reflects a sustained effort to compile Alma Cristobal’s certified medical records and related billing, including updates to capture post-August follow-up visits and the necessary certification pages, with communications spanning from July 2024 through September 2024, and a final clarification and reminder on January 21, 2025 about missing early visits ([DOB-116], [DOB-117], and [DOB-118]) requiring inclusion in the certified package.

item_61.note: This note concerns the case Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024, involving client Alma Cristobal, with the matter titled Certified Medical Records & Billing Request - Alma Cristobal. The Whaley Law Firm represents the client, and the communications are with Starlight (also referred to as Starlite) Chiropractic. The December 11, 2024 email was sent by Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers' Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, to Gail at Starlight Chiropractic, with two Starlight addresses included ([EMAIL-131] and [EMAIL-344]), and with CCs to Aaron Whaley ([EMAIL-343]) and Muhammad Alif ([EMAIL-342]). The message was dated Wednesday, December 11, 2024, at 13:44:57 -0500.

In this December 11 communication, Sarena stated that they still had not received the Certification page for the attached records and bills that had been discussed on October 7, 2024. She explained that if a claim is in litigation, they cannot file the records or bills with the courts without a completed, signed certification page. She added that if the proper certification is not received, the treatment and/or bills cannot be considered for payment, and she urged Gail to expedite the required certification as soon as possible. The message included The Whaley Law Firm’s standard signature block, noting the new email address and providing direct and office phone numbers, along with the firm’s mailing address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222.

The chain also shows prior correspondence. On October 7, 2024, at approximately 11:46 AM, Sarena Tuttle wrote, “Please find the CRR w/Certification Page Attached,” followed by the same signature block and contact information, including the note about the new email address. Before that, a forwarded message from July 23, 2024, at 2:21 PM, indicated that Sarena had sent an email to Starlite Chiropractic (and [EMAIL-341]) with the subject Certified Medical Records & Billing Request - Alma Cristobal. In that July message, she stated: “Good afternoon Gail, Please find attached our office's request for certified medical records and billing on the above referenced client. If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to contact us directly to discuss them in further detail.” The signature block following that message again listed Sarena M. Tuttle’s role, the firm’s address, direct and office phone numbers, the email contact, and the note to use the new email address.

Taken together, the record shows a sequence of communications from The Whaley Law Firm to Starlight/Starlite Chiropractic regarding certified medical records and billing for Alma Cristobal, culminating in a December 11, 2024 email stressing that the critical Certification page has not been received since the October 7, 2024 discussion, and outlining the consequences for filing and payment if the certification is not provided promptly.

item_68.note: In the case of Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corpora, docketed as Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024, the parties moved to schedule the deposition of Roy Hamilton after the initial written discovery had been completed. On November 21, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Nichole M. Priddy of Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC (cc’ing Aletha N. Thomas and Bryce Koon) asking for dates that Mr. Hamilton and the offices could be available for deposition. The subject line of that message referenced the matter as 108134 : [PHONE-323] : Cristobal, Alma v. Crete Carrier Corpora : Alma Cristobal v Crete Carrier & Roy Hamilton - Deposition Scheduling. In that note, Sarena wrote, “Good afternoon. It appears the initial written discovery has been completed by both parties and we are ready to move forward with scheduling the deposition of Mr. Roy Hamilton. Can you (or Nicole) please provide dates that your office and Mr. Hamilton are available for deposition?”

Later that same day, November 21, 2024, Nichole replied that Aletha’s calendar was quite booked from now until after the first of the year and proposed the weeks of February 3–7 and February 10–14 as potential windows. Nichole also noted that Aletha would want to take the deposition of Ms. Cristobal as well and asked to be informed of Cristobal’s availability within that timeframe; she said she would contact Mr. Hamilton to coordinate dates for all parties. The message was signed with Nichole’s contact information and standard confidentiality notice.

On November 22, 2024 at 9:06 a.m., Sarena responded, suggesting that they look at the week of February 3–7 since they were already pushing things out and that Ms. Cristobal would be available that week as well. She asked Nichole to let them know what would work best for Kopka Pinkus Dolin and Mr. Hamilton.

On November 26, 2024, at 9:29 a.m., Nichole informed Sarena that she had heard back from Mr. Hamilton and that February 5, 2025 would be good for him, with the deposition to be held via Zoom.

Later that morning, at 10:53 a.m., Sarena responded that February 5, 2025 via Zoom was perfect and asked for guidance on timing. She proposed starting at 10:00 a.m. with Ms. Cristobal and beginning Mr. Hamilton’s deposition at 1:00 p.m. to allow time for lunch, or alternatively proceeding immediately after Ms. Cristobal’s deposition. She signed off with her title and contact details, noting her new Whaley Law Firm email address.

At 1:18 p.m. on the same day, Nichole replied that the suggested plan sounded good and that she was not sure how much time Aletha would need, but she agreed with the proposed timing. Her message also carried Kopka Pinkus Dolin’s standard confidentiality notice and her contact information.

Finally, at 2:14 p.m., Sarena sent a closing note confirming that she would obtain a deposition notice for Mr. Hamilton and send it over shortly, with her usual signature block and new email address.

In summary, after confirming that initial discovery had been completed, the team settled on scheduling the deposition of Roy Hamilton for February 5, 2025, via Zoom, with Ms. Cristobal’s deposition included in the same window. They discussed starting times—10:00 a.m. for Cristobal and 1:00 p.m. for Hamilton to allow for lunch, or proceeding consecutively—depending on the time Aletha Thomas would need. The coordinated dates were set within the week of February 3–7, 2025, within the broader February 3–14, 2025 timeframe, with Mr. Hamilton’s availability confirmed for February 5.

item_70.note: Case: Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024
Client: Alma Cristobal

In the matter of Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corp. and Roy Hamilton (108134: [PHONE-322]), deposition scheduling correspondence occurred between Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC and The Whaley Law Firm in late November 2024. The client is Alma Cristobal.

On November 21, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, wrote to Aletha N. Thomas and Nichole M. Priddy requesting dates for deposition of Mr. Roy Hamilton, noting that the initial written discovery had been completed by both parties and that they were ready to move forward with scheduling. Nichole M. Priddy, a legal assistant at Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC and assistant to Aletha Thomas and Kristin Lomond, replied later that day. She explained that Aletha’s calendar was booked from now until after the first of the year and, after reviewing Aletha’s calendar, proposed the weeks of February 3–7 and February 10–14 as potential windows. Nichole added that Aletha would also want to depose Ms. Cristobal and asked for Cristobal’s availability during that timeframe. She stated she would contact Mr. Hamilton to determine dates that would work for him so the deposition scheduling could be coordinated for all parties.

The following day, November 22, 2024, Sarena Tuttle responded, suggesting the week of February 3–7 as a practical focus given how far out the scheduling had become. She noted that Ms. Cristobal would be available that week as well and asked Nichole and her office to indicate what dates worked best for their side and for Mr. Hamilton.

On November 26, 2024, Nichole M. Priddy informed Sarena that she had heard back from Mr. Hamilton, and he advised that February 5, 2025, would be suitable for his deposition, to be conducted via Zoom. This established a concrete date for the deposition of Roy Hamilton, with the expectation that the deposition of Alma Cristobal would also be arranged within the same scheduling window.

The correspondence indicates ongoing coordination to schedule the deposition of Roy Hamilton, with Aletha Thomas also intending to depose Alma Cristobal, within the suggested weeks of February 3–7 and February 10–14, 2025, and with Mr. Hamilton’s availability confirmed for February 5, 2025, by Zoom. The exchange involved the principals and paralegals at Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC and The Whaley Law Firm, respectively, to finalize a mutually workable deposition schedule for all parties.

item_71.note: Narrative summary of deposition scheduling communications for Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corp. and Roy Hamilton (Case: Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024)

The parties, Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corp. and Roy Hamilton, began coordinating the deposition of Mr. Roy Hamilton after the initial written discovery had been completed by both sides. On November 21, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager with The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Nichole M. Priddy of Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC (cc’ing Aletha N. Thomas and Bryce Koon) to announce that the parties were ready to move forward with scheduling Mr. Hamilton’s deposition and to request dates when their offices and Mr. Hamilton would be available.

Later on November 21, 2024 at 3:08 PM, Nichole replied that Aletha’s calendar was pretty booked from now until after the first of the year and proposed scheduling for the weeks of February 3–7 and February 10–14. Nichole noted that Aletha would also want to depose Ms. Cristobal and she would check with Mr. Hamilton to confirm dates that would work for all parties.

On November 22, 2024 at 9:06 AM, Sarena responded that they could look at the week of February 3–7 since they were already pushing out the schedule, and that Ms. Cristobal would be available that week. She asked Nichole to let them know what dates worked best for Kopka Pinkus Dolin and Mr. Hamilton, and she indicated they would accommodate accordingly.

Subsequently, on November 26, 2024 at 9:29 AM, Nichole informed that Mr. Hamilton had advised February 5, 2025 would be good for him, and that the deposition would be conducted via Zoom.

That same day, November 26, 2024 at 10:52 AM, Sarena replied that February 5, 2025 via Zoom was perfect. She added a logistical question about timing: she asked how much time Mrs. Thomas would need, or typically takes, and proposed two possible schedules. One option was to start at 10:00 a.m. with Ms. Cristobal and to have Mr. Hamilton begin at 1:00 p.m. to allow time for lunch; alternatively, they could proceed immediately following the Cristobal deposition. She provided her contact information and signed off with her title and firm details. The overall plan remained to conduct the deposition of Mr. Roy Hamilton via Zoom on February 5, 2025, with Ms. Cristobal’s deposition to occur in the surrounding time window, subject to the parties’ schedules.

Priddy of Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC (along with Aletha N. Priddy cc’d and Alma Cristobal’s Filevine project email address also included in the cc list ([EMAIL-208]). The subject of the message referenced the matter as 108134: [PHONE-209]: Cristobal, Alma v. Crete Carrier Corpora: Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corporation, et al. (Jefferson 24-CI-004728). Koon’s message stated that he was following up on discovery requests served to Defendant Crete and requested any updates. The email included The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and a standard confidentiality disclaimer, noting that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain attorney-client privileged information; if received in error, the recipient should contact the firm and refrain from using or forwarding the information. The message also contained a note indicating that the email had been scanned for threats by Mimecast, and included Kopka Pinkus Dolin’s confidentiality notice.

On October 9, 2024, at 3:42? PM, Aletha N. Thomas responded. She thanked Bryce for the email and his patience and advised that she was awaiting her client’s verification of the responses and would transmit them as soon as she received them. Her signature block identified her as a partner at Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC, with office locations in Louisville; her contact details, and a standard confidentiality disclaimer similar to the one included in the prior message.

On November 1, 2024, at approximately 12:08 p.m., Bryce Koon, Esq., again wrote to Aletha Thomas and others, attaching the motion. He closed with his contact information for The Whaley Law Firm. The message included the same standard attorney-client privilege language and confidentiality notices, and reiterated the firm’s disclaimer about privileged information and the proper handling of the email if received in error. The email chain also included Alma Cristobal’s Filevine project email address in the cc list: [EMAIL-210].

Earlier in the chain, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent a separate note on November 1, 2024 at 2:02 p.m. to Bryce Koon and others. She advised that the motion hour had been moved by the clerk to November 12, 2024, due to Veterans Day on November 11. Her message included her contact details, including direct dial and office phone numbers, her new email address (Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com), and The Whaley Law Firm’s address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222). Her signature also indicated she provided the update in her capacity as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager. The email again carried standard confidentiality and privilege notices, including a reminder not to use or forward the information if received in error, and noting that it had been scanned for threats by Mimecast.

In sum, the record reflects an ongoing discovery process regarding defendant Crete in the Alma Cristobal v. Crete Carrier Corporation matter, with initial follow-ups on discovery in early October, a motion email in early November indicating a hearing set for November 11 at 9:45 a.m. (subject to remand if client responses were received beforehand), and a clerk-led rescheduling notice moving the hearing to November 12, 2024 due to Veterans Day. Aletha N. Thomas, in an email dated October 9, 2024 at 3:42 PM, responded to Bryce. item_103.last_activity: 2024-10-15T00:00:00
item_103.note: This note concerns Case Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024 and the client Alma Cristobal. On October 15, 2024, at 14:11:33 UTC, Louisville Metro Government Public Records sent an external message regarding public records request #24-12999 to sarena@whaleylawfirm.com. The request sought body and dash camera video responsive to the inquiry.

The Public Records unit states that they located video responsive to the request, and that this record is not otherwise available. They need additional time to prepare the records for release. An extension is necessary because the requested records were created during the course of police business and are expected to contain a mixture of exempt and non-exempt information. The exempt information is likely of a personal nature related to the involved person(s) or CJIS-protected information, which is prohibited from release.

The message explains the process the unit follows to research, locate, and redact body/dash camera video requests. Currently, the unit has four members who are responsible for the department’s open records requests involving body/dash camera video and any audio/video included in case file requests. For each request, staff must search by officer and date. If video is located, they must determine whether an investigation or court case related to the incident is open. They then download each video one at a time, watch it, and manually redact any exempt information to protect citizens’ privacy and to meet CJIS security requirements. There is no automatic redaction; only one item, image, or sound may be redacted at a time, so multiple exempt items must be redacted individually. For every minute of video, it is estimated to take seven minutes to redact and review. Consequently, some requests take as little as 30 minutes to an hour, while others can take over a week. A single request does not necessarily correspond to a single video, as some requests may involve two, five, ten, or more videos.

Based on these factors, and pursuant to KRS 61.872(5), the non-exempt responsive records will be made available on or before March 7, 2025. To remain fair and unbiased, the unit processes requests in the order they are received. They currently have an estimated 1,000+ pending requests for video and are working as diligently as possible given the resources and personnel allocated. If a request is completed earlier than the quoted date, it will be provided sooner. The notice also notes that video may be provided faster via subpoena if applicable.

For questions about the request, you may reply to the email or sign in to contact staff at Louisville Metro Government. Technical support is available via the help page.

item_129.note: Case: Alma Cristobal, assigned to the Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024 file, concerns a new appointment request for the client Alma Cristobal related to her February 15, 2024 motor vehicle accident (MVA). The communications are between Aptiva Health and The Whaley Law Firm, with multiple recipients and copies.

On August 26, 2024, Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, reported that Mrs. Cristobal had stopped by the office and described ongoing issues with her left shoulder and upper extremity. She stated there is continuous pain in the left shoulder that radiates down her side and sometimes into her left arm all the way to her first digit. She also noted puffiness in the clavicle region, although there was no discoloration at that time. Sarena requested that someone reach out to Mrs. Cristobal to schedule a follow-up appointment and to consider MRI imaging.

Later that same day, August 26, 2024 at 3:54 PM, April Mullins, an A/R Specialist / Lien Negotiator and Attorney Liaison at Aptiva Health, replied to Sarena with a question: Is this still under Mrs. Cristobal’s 2/15/24 MVA? In her signature she identified herself and provided her contact information and company details, including that she had included Aptiva Health’s call center team to confirm appointment information once scheduling occurs.

On August 27, 2024 at 9:43 AM, Sarena responded to April with, “Good morning April, Yes, it is,” confirming that the case remains tied to the 2/15/24 MVA.

That same day, August 27, 2024 at 1:51 PM, April replied, “We can work on getting her back in. I have included our call center team who can confirm appointment information once she’s scheduled.”

The chain of communication also notes that the initial exchange carried the subject Alma Cristobal – New Appointment Request, and that Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm were CC’d, along with the Aptiva Health CallCenter. The parties and contact details referenced include Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm (713 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) with direct line [PHONE-283], office line [PHONE-284] ext 104, and email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting a new email address). For Aptiva Health, April Mullins’s information lists Office [PHONE-285], Cell [PHONE-286], [EMAIL-287], aptivahealth.com, and the address 12300 Plantside Dr, Louisville, KY 40299, with the call center email [EMAIL-288].

item_134.note: Case: Alma Cristobal (Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024) involves a new appointment request for the client Alma Cristobal. Over the dates of August 26–27, 2024, The Whaley Law Firm and Aptiva Health exchanged a series of messages to address follow-up care after a motor vehicle accident and to arrange an appointment, including consideration of MRI imaging if indicated.

On Monday, August 26, 2024, at 3:40 PM, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, informed April Mullins that Mrs. Cristobal had visited the office that day and reported ongoing issues with her left shoulder and upper extremity. She described continuous pain in the left shoulder that radiates down the side and sometimes into the left arm all the way to the first digit, with puffiness in the clavicle region though there was no discoloration at this time. Sarena requested that someone follow up with the patient to schedule an appointment and consider possible MRI imaging.

At 3:54 PM later that day, April Mullins replied, asking whether this is still under the 2/15/24 motor vehicle accident. She noted that follow-up would be arranged and included her contact information along with Aptiva Health’s call center details, as well as the office address: Aptiva Health, 12300 Plantside Dr, Louisville, KY 40299. Her message carried her signature block with office and cell numbers (Office: [PHONE-297]; Cell: [PHONE-298]), email [EMAIL-299], and the website aptivahealth.com. The email also contained standard confidentiality language and images indicated by embedded cid attachments.

Earlier the same day, at 9:43 AM, Sarena Tuttle replied to April: “Good morning April, Yes, it is,” confirming that the matter remained under the 2/15/24 MVA.

In another exchange at 9:51 AM on Tuesday, August 27, 2024, April Mullins wrote back: “We can work on getting her back in. I have included our call center team who can confirm appointment information once she’s scheduled.” This message also included April’s standard contact information and confidentiality notice.

At 10:11 AM on August 27, 2024, Sarena Tuttle responded: “Awesome. Thank you so much,” indicating appreciation for the plan to schedule the appointment.

Finally, at 3:42 PM on Tuesday, August 27, 2024, Lisa Acton sent an email to Sarena Tuttle and April Mullins, with Greg Whaley, Bryce Koon, and CallCenter CC’d. The subject was in reference to Alma Cristobal’s new appointment request, and the body stated, “Good morning, this patient has been scheduled for an appointment today with our provider. Thank you and have a good day!” This message confirms that an appointment was scheduled for the patient, with the call center to confirm appointment details.

In summary, the timeline shows the patient presenting with persistent left shoulder and upper-extremity pain after a February 15, 2024 motor vehicle accident, concerns about possible MRI imaging, and a coordinated effort between The Whaley Law Firm and Aptiva Health to schedule an appointment for August 27, 2024, after confirming the case remains under the MVA, and arranging call-center support for appointment confirmation.

item_145.note: This note covers communications in the Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024 case, involving client Alma Cristobal and related counsel and entities. The matter is titled Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024 with the client listed as Alma Cristobal, and it concerns a February 15, 2024 accident involving Crete Carrier Corpora (as reflected in the subject lines of the exchanged emails).

On August 6, 2024, Aletha N. Thomas, a Partner at Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC, wrote to Bryce Koon and Nichole M. Priddy. In that email, she stated she had been retained to represent Crete Carrier Corporation and Roy Hamilton regarding the February 15, 2024 accident. She believed Bryce Koon represented Alma Cristobal. Aletha attached a copy of the Answer she had just filed on behalf of Crete Carrier Corporation. She noted that Mr. Hamilton had not yet been served, but she would file an Answer on his behalf once he was served. She also indicated that she understood discovery requests had been propounded with the Complaint and asked Bryce to send her a copy of those discovery requests in Word format. The email included Aletha’s contact information and firm details: Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC, 462 South Fourth Street, Suite 101, Louisville, KY 40202, with telephone numbers and office locations in Illinois, Indiana, Michigan, Kentucky, and Wisconsin. A confidentiality notice accompanied the message, stating that the email may contain confidential information and, if received by an unintended recipient, review, copying, or distribution is prohibited; recipients were asked to destroy the original transmittal and notify the sender. It also provided a standard firm disclaimer and contact links and noted that the firm’s office was moving.

The same August 6 email contained a firm signature block for Aletha N. Thomas and reiterated the relocation information. It stated that the Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC offices would be relocating effective August 28 to 101 South Fifth Street, Suite 1670, Louisville, KY 40202, while Aletha’s email address, telephone number, and fax number would remain the same. On August 23, 2024 at approximately 8:24 PM (note: the timestamp is recorded as 8:24?PM in the forwarding), Aletha followed up with Bryce Koon regarding the same matter. She wrote to Bryce, with Nichole M. Priddy CC’d, asking him to send her the discovery requests to Crete in Word format. The body of the message read: “Hi, Bryce, Just following up on this. Could you please send me the discovery requests to Crete in Word format? Thank you!” The email again carried Aletha’s Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC signature block, including their Louisville address and relocation notice, and included the confidentiality notice.

This August 23 email was part of a chain that was later forwarded. On August 24, 2024 at 09:16:19 AM, Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm forwarded the chain to Sarena Tuttle. The forwarded content began with the same headers and included the August 23, 2024 message from Aletha N. Thomas, as described above. The forward shows the Whaley Law Firm’s contact information: 712 Lyndon Ln, Louisville, KY 40222, [PHONE-315], and the “Forwarded message” header and related copy of Aletha’s email.

In sum, the exchanged communications document Crete Carrier Corporation’s representation by Aletha N. Thomas in connection with the February 15, 2024 accident, the status of service on Roy Hamilton, the existence of discovery requests associated with the Complaint, and Aletha’s request to receive those discovery requests in Word format. They also establish that Bryce Koon may represent Alma Cristobal, that Aletha had filed an Answer on Crete’s behalf, and that Hamilton’s responsive pleading would follow upon service. The emails also provide Kopka Pinkus Dolin PC’s contact details, the firm’s relocation to a new Louisville address, and standard confidentiality notices, along with a forwarded chain that includes Whaley Law Firm’s involvement.

item_180.note: Case: Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024. Client: Alma Cristobal.

On May 23, 2024, Jessa Galosmo of Whaley Law Firm forwarded to Alma Cristobal’s Filevine project email address a message titled “FW: Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request.” The forwarded note begins with the line: “No records from Mary and Elizabeth Hospital but with UofL hospital.”

The forwarded chain then contains a message from May 22, 2024 at about 5:48 PM in the “Itemized Bills” thread, sent to Jessa Galosmo with the subject “FW: Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request.” That message itself was a forwarding of a prior message from ULH Customer Service.

The original ULH message was sent on April 2, 2024 at 2:44 PM to Itemized Bills, with the subject “FW: Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request.” It was authored by Robinlynn Brown, a Customer Service Specialist in Accounts Receivable Operation, whose email address is [EMAIL-383]. The message includes a lengthy description of UofL Health, Inc.: it is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit corporation governed by an independent Board of Directors, and it is a related organization to the University of Louisville’s School of Medicine (defined under 42 CFR 413.17). UofL Health, Inc., on behalf of its teaching hospitals and providers, has an academic affiliation agreement with the University of Louisville whereby the University’s Health Sciences Center serves as the academic partner to maintain and enhance graduate medical education and its related research.

The message also contains a Confidentiality Disclaimer stating that the email and attachments are confidential and may contain protected health information (PHI) under HIPAA; if you are not the intended recipient, dissemination or copying is prohibited, and recipients should notify the sender or contact the UofL Health IT Service Desk at [PHONE-384] if the message was received in error.

In the April 2, 2024 ULH message, the sender addressed to Jessa: “Hi Jessa, We do not have any accounts for the dates request where patient was seen at Mary and Elizabeth Hospital. We do show patient was at UofL Hospital. Please respond with an updated request and authorization and I will gladly send to you. Thanks! Brenda S.”

Within the same thread, before the April 2 correspondence, the chain shows a prior message from Jessa Galosmo sent on Friday, March 29, 2024 at 10:57 AM to ULH Customer Service with the subject “Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request.” That March 29 message contains a security notice: “SECURITY ALERT! This message is from an outside sender! Please review with caution and only open links you know are safe. Please click the ‘Report Phishing’ button on your tool bar to report this message to the security team for review.” The body of Jessa’s message is brief: “Hi, Please see attached file.” It is signed with all the standard closing lines from Jessa Galosmo of Whaley Law Firm, including contact information: Ph: [PHONE-385] and Fax: [PHONE-386].

In summary, the correspondence centers on an Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño bill request. The ULH response indicates there were no accounts for the dates when the patient was seen at Mary and Elizabeth Hospital, but records show the patient was at UofL Hospital, and an updated request with authorization was requested in order to proceed. The May 23 forwarding note explicitly records the statement that there were no Mary and Elizabeth Hospital records, only records at UofL Hospital. The attachments mentioned in the March 29 email are not shown in this note, but the message confirms that Jessa had sent an attachment and followed up with ULH accordingly.

On March 29, 2024, Jessa Galosmo of Whaley Law Firm sent an email to ULH Customer Service with the subject Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request and, in the thread, to the Filevine project email address for Ala Cristobal ([EMAIL-414]). The message from Jessa included the line “Hi, Please see attached file,” and carried Jessa’s firm signature block, including the phone and fax numbers, with the closing “All the best, Jessa Galosmo” and the firm’s contact information.

The forwarded chain shows a response from ULH Customer Service dated April 2, 2024, around 2:44 PM, addressed to Jessa Galosmo. The reply stated: “We have received your request, please allow 30-45 for processing before calling for an update or sending another request as that may delay the first request. Thank You.” The message was signed by Robinlynn Brown, Customer Service Specialist, Accounts Receivable Operation, and included her contact email [EMAIL-415].

The ULH message also contained organizational background text describing UofL Health, Inc. as a 501(c)(3) nonprofit corporation governed by an independent Board of Directors. It explained that UofL Health, Inc. is a related organization with the University of Louisville’s School of Medicine, and that, under an academic affiliation agreement, the University of Louisville serves as the academic partner with UofL Health, Inc. to maintain and enhance affiliated graduate medical education as well as its research in medicine, dentistry, nursing, and public health. A confidentiality disclaimer followed, noting that the message and any attachments are confidential and may contain information privileged or exempt from disclosure under applicable law, including Protected Health Information (PHI) under HIPAA. It advised that if you were not the intended recipient, dissemination, distribution, or copying of the message is prohibited, and to report receipt to the sender or to the UofL Health IT Service Desk at [PHONE-416].

The chain also shows the original message from Jessa Galosmo to ULH Customer Service dated Friday, March 29, 2024 at 10:57 AM, subject Alma Socorro Cristobal Avendaño-Bill request. That message included a prominent security-alert banner warning that the message is from an outside sender and advising caution, including instructions to review links carefully and to click the “Report Phishing” button to notify the security team. The body of the March 29 email simply stated, “Hi, Please see attached file.” It was signed by Jessa Galosmo, Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s phone and fax numbers, followed by a second closing line of “All the best, Jessa Galosmo” and the same contact details.

item_207.note: Case: Alma-Cristobal-MVA-2-15-2024. Client: Alma Cristobal.

On April 1, 2024, an email thread concerning the liability decision for claim [PHONE-422] and the acknowledgement of a letter of representation (sent March 27, 2024) circulated between Jessa Galosmo of the Whaley Law Firm and Brenna Rine, a liability adjuster for transportation claims handling Crete Carrier Corporation, Shaffer Trucking, and Hunt Transportation Inc. The thread began with an email from Jessa Galosmo. At 7:13 AM she wrote to Brenna, stating she was following up on the liability decision for the claim and the acknowledgement for the letter of representation that had been sent on March 27, 2024. She signed as Jessa Galosmo of the Whaley Law Firm, providing her phone number [PHONE-423] and fax number [PHONE-424], and included a confidentiality notice indicating the transmission is privileged and confidential and should be delivered only to the named addressee(s). The notice also warned recipients that if they were not the intended recipient, they should notify the sender and delete the communication from their system, and that the material should not be copied, stored, or retained without consent.

The following portion of the thread shows a reply from Brenna Rine, dated April 1, 2024, at about 10:40 AM. In her reply, Brenna indicated, “Please see attached letters. Thank you,” and she provided her professional contact information: Liability Adjuster for Transportation Claims at 400 NW 56th Street, Lincoln, NE 68528, representing Crete Carrier Corporation, Shaffer Trucking, and Hunt Transportation Inc. Her office phone was [PHONE-425], with fax [PHONE-426], and her email was [EMAIL-427].

Later that same day, at 11:28:41 AM, the thread was forwarded to Alma Cristobal’s Filevine project email address, with the subject “Fwd: [PHONE-428].” The forwarded message retained the prior content: it was from Jessa Galosmo, and it included the header information showing the original recipient as the Filevine project email address and the date of the forward. The body of the forwarded message echoed Brenna’s prior note, “Please see attached letters,” and again carried Brenna’s signature block and the attached-letter reference.

In addition to the substantive exchanges, the messages include standard email cautions and disclosures. Jessa’s initial message contains the caution that the email originated outside the organization and advises not to click links or open attachments unless the sender and content are known to be safe. The thread also includes a confidentiality disclaimer common to such communications, stating that the transmission is privileged and confidential and intended only for the named addressee(s), with instructions for notification and deletion if received by the wrong party. The communications also repeat the contact information for both Jessa Galosmo of Whaley Law Firm and Brenna Rine of Trans Claims, as well as the associated companies involved in the claim.
